The Eternal Nature of Command and Prohibition: Hanafi vs. Ash'ari
Expansion of the dispute on the temporality of command and prohibition in Allah's speech

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Abdullah ibn Sa'id al-Qattan's Ash'ari view that command and prohibition are not eternal in Allah's speech, evaluate the Hanafi critique based on the impossibility of a divided without divisions, and state the thamarah al-khilaf regarding the nature of obligation.

Core Idea
Allah's speech is one eternal attribute; command and prohibition become actual only when relation to an act occurs.

This lesson examines a key usul dispute about Allah's attribute of speech: are 'command' and 'prohibition' eternal divisions of that speech, or do they arise only temporally? The Ash'ari scholar Abdullah ibn Sa'id al-Qattan argued that in eternity, Allah's speech is a common factor (mushtarak) without any specific division, and that command and prohibition are temporal accidents that occur later when relations (ta'alluqat) to acts exist. The Hanafi school responds that even if divisions are accidents, the existence of a divided (like speech) without some division is impossible. This debate has implications for understanding taklif (obligation) of non-existent beings and the attribute of speech itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Issue
Determine the precise point of disagreement: whether Allah's speech in eternity is actually command or prohibition, or merely a potential that becomes actual later. The Mu'tazilite objection about foolishness (safah) and frivolity ('abath) is the background.
The Mu'tazila argued that an eternal command to a non-existent being would be meaningless, so either speech is temporal or command is not eternal.
2
State al-Qattan's Position and His Dalil
Summarize al-Qattan's view: in eternity, speech has no relation (ta'alluq) to any act, so it is not actually command or prohibition. The eternal aspect is the common factor, while divisions are originated (haditha). His dalil: avoiding the necessity of addressing non-existents, which would imply foolishness.
Al-Qattan was a leading Ash'ari, considered advanced over al-Ash'ari himself.
3
Explain the Hanafi Objection
The Hanafi author argues that the existence of a divided (muqassam) without any division is impossible. Even if divisions are accidents, they must still exist in some form. Al-Qattan's claim that the common factor is eternal without any division leads to a contradiction (khulf).
The Hanafi position is that speech is one eternal attribute, but it is inherently such that it will be command/prohibition when relation occurs.
4
Analyze the Resolution
The author suggests that al-Qattan's view can be reconciled with the majority if we interpret his negation of command/prohibition as referring to actual (munajjaz) command/prohibition, not the potential. Thus, the speech is eternally suitable (salih) for command/prohibition, but actualization occurs in time.
This shows that the dispute is largely terminological; both sides agree on conditional obligation (taklif ta'liqi).
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: whether the divine address is eternal or temporal; whether the attribute of speech is one or multiple; and the nature of obligation for non-existent beings.
The Hanafi view preserves the unity and eternality of the attribute while allowing for temporal multiplicity in relation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوده مع في ۱۱۹ المقالة الثانية في الأحكام في «التوراة» قبل أن يخلق آدم بأربعين سنة : ﴿ وَعَصَى عَادَمُ رَبَّهُ فَعَوَى ) [طه: ١٢١]، وهذا خبر من غير متعلق، وهو كذب فما هو جوابكم، فهو جوابنا قلنا: إنما يلزم ذلك) أي السفه والعبث (لو كان الطلب في الأزل تنجيزاً ولا نقول به أما لو كان ممن سيكون معلقاً على صفة التكليف (فلا يلزم كأمر) الرسول صلوات الله عليه وآله وأصحابه أجمعين (في حقنا وبذلك اندفع ما قيل إنه لا يصح تعلق التكليف بالمعدوم، كيف لا وإن تحقق التعلق بدون المتعلق ممتنع ضرورة أن الإضافة لا تتحقق بدون المضاف إليه) والتعلق إضافة بين الآمر والمأمور (وذلك) الاندفاع (لأن الامتناع المذكور في التعلق التنجيزي، وأما العقلي فلا يحتاج إلى تحقق المضاف إليه إذ ليس تعلقاً متحققاً بالفعل فيكفي له العلم فتدبر) فإنه جليّ وينكر (قيل) في الجواب السفه والعبث من صفات الأفعال ولا يتصف بهما الكيف والكلام النفسي من الصفات) دون الأفعال (فلا يتصف بهما فلزوم السفه والعبث ممنوع (أقول) لا بل يتصف بهما بعض الصفات أيضاً، كيف لا والأمر طلب، والطلب يتصف بهما إجماعاً، اعلم أن عبد الله بن سعيد القطان (من) (الأشاعرة أي من أهل السنة والجماعة، وكان مقدماً على الأشعري (ذهب مستخلصاً عن هذا اللزوم) لزوم السفه والعبث (إلى أن كلامه تعالى (ليس الأزل أمراً أو نهياً أو غيرهما من الإخبار والاستفهام، بل يتصف بهذه فيما لا يزال بعد حدوث التعلقات والمتعلقات بل القديم هو الأمر المشترك بينهما ( والأقسام حادثة) وقد رأيت كتب بعض المحدثين أنهم حكموا بكون هذا الرأي مختاراً (وأورد عليه أن هذه الأشياء من الأمر والنهي وغيرهما (أنواع ) للكلام (ويستحيل وجود الجنس إلا في ضمن نوع (ما) فلا يتصور قدم المشترك (وأجاب) عبد الله بن سعيد (بمنع أنها أنواعه بل إنها (عوارضه بحسب) عروض (التعلق) وهو حادث ويجوز خلوه عنه وكان في الأزل غير متعلق فلا يكون فيه أمراً ونهياً، ويمكن الاستناد بأن كلامه تعالى واحد معين فلا يكون جنساً صادقاً على الحقائق المختلفة (أقول) : هذا الجواب غير تام فإنا سلمنا أنها ليست أنواعاً لكن لا شك في أنها أقسام و(وجود المقسم بدون وجود (قسم ما محال وإن كان التقسيم باعتبار العوارض) وإذ قد قال بوجود المقسم بدون هذه العوارض فيلزم عليه القول بوجود قسم ما بدون هذه العوارض وهو) باطل (لا يعقل مع أنه يلزم خلاف الفرض إذ قال : إن القديم هو المشترك هذا خلف فتدبر) اعلم أن كلامه تعالى واحد أزلي لا اختلاف فيه في ذاته ولا انقسام بل إنما يتعدد وينقسم بتعدد التعلقات، وبما قال القطان إنه ليس في الأزل تعلق فلا تعدد ولا انقسام، نعم هو صالح، لأن يتعدد فيما لا يزال بعروض التعلقات المتعددة، نعم لو كان كلياً صادقاً على الكثير لا يمكن وجوده بدون قسم ما وهذا ظاهر جداً، فحينئذ قوله : وجود المقسم بدون قسم ما محال ممنوع، وإن خصص بالمقسم الكلي فغير نافع، ولعل هذا هو معنى ما في «الحاشية» أنه فرق بين التقسيم بالعوارض وبينه بعد عروض العوارض وها هنا التقسيم من القبيل الثاني وعروض العوارض فيما لا يزال، فوجود المقسم بدون الأقسام فيما لا يزال محال، لكن الحق أن المعنى المقصود فيه التخاطب لا يعقل وجوده بدون قسم ما ولا يخفى أن قصد التخاطب في مطلقاً ۱۲۰ فواتح الرحموت شرح مسلم الثبوت الجزء الأول بالفعل البتة يستدعي وجود الأقسام، وأما قصد التخاطب فيما سيكون فلا يستدعي إلا تحقق الأقسام فيه، والسر فيه أن التخاطب لا يكون إلا في التعلق التنجيزي فلا تعلق في الأزل إلا بمعنى صحة الإفادة لا غير، وهو لا يستدعي الأقسام بالفعل، ولك أن تقول إنه سبحانه وتعالى يعلم في الأزل المكلفين بأعيانهم ، وأنهم في وقت وجودهم بشرائط التكليف مأمورون بكذا وممنوعون عن كذا أو لا يعلم وعلى الثاني يلزم أن لا يتحقق التكليف فيما لا يزال أيضاً: لأنه لم يعلم الله ذلك وهو باطل، فتعين الأول فثبت الأمر والنهي العقليان فلزم وجود قسم ما وأيضاً لا يكون المعدوم حينئذ مكلفاً) أي حين وجد الكلام ولم يصر أمراً ونهياً ولا شيئاً من الأقسام، إذ لا تعلق للكلام بفعل المكلف حينئذ، وقد يجاب عنه بالتزام عدم كون المعدوم مكلفاً عنده وهو فاسد، لأن اعتراض السفه والعبث إنما كان على تجويز تكليف المعدوم إذ عند إنكار ذلك لا توجه للإيراد، فلا يصح الاستخلاص عنه بهذا الوجه، وقد كان القطان إنما قال هذا الكلام مستخلصاً عن الإيراد المذكور، إلا أن يقال : المعتزلة كانوا يوردون اعتراض السفه والعبث على قدم الكلام فاستخلص بهذا، والحق أنه لا خلاف بينه وبين الجمهور في أزلية التكليف التعليقي، كما قال مطلع الأسرار الإلهية لعله أراد بالأمر والنهي المنفيين الأمر والنهي المنجزين، فحينئذ يرجع إلى ما ذهب إليه الجمهور، وحينئذ لا شبهة في أن عروض هذه العوارض فيما لا يزال قطعاً، وعلى هذا لا يرد عليه شيء من الوجوه المذكورة (و) المعتزلة (قالوا) لو كان الخطاب أزلياً (يلزم قدم عدم التناهي) فإن المعدومين غير متناه، فكذا ما هو متعلق بهم من الخطاب فإن المتعلق بزيد غير المتعلق بعمرو والجواب) أن لا تعدد في الخطاب المتعلق بالذات (وإن التعدد العارض له بحسب تعدد التعلقات تعدد اعتباري فإنه أي الخطاب (صفة واحدة أزلية لا تعدد فيه كالعلم والقدرة، وانقسامه إلى الأنواع والأفراد بحسب التعلقات لا باختلاف الذاتيات كانقسامها (هذا) فإن قلت هب أن التعدد فيه بحسب اعتباري، لكن التعلقات ليست اختراعية محضة بل لها حظ من الثبوت الواقعي والإلزام كون الأوامر والنواهي اختراعية فيلزم فيها التسلسل، قلت : معنى كونها واقعية أن الخطاب إذا قيس إلى متعلقه صالح لأن ينتزع عنه التعلق ،لا أن التعلق أمر موجود في التعين فتأمل، ثم الإشكال من الأصل لأن المكلفين محصورون بين وجود آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام وبين القيامة، فهم متناهون، وكذا التعلقات فتأمل فيه، وقالوا ثانياً لو كان الكلام أزلياً لاستوى نسبته إلى الكل، والحسن والقبح عندكم شرعي، فهو صالح لأن يتعلق بكل شيء، فيلزم أن يتعلق الأمر والنهي بفعل واحد قلنا لا نسلم أن الحسن والقبح شرعيان بل الأشياء بعضها حسنة وبعضها قبيحة، فيتعلق الأمر بذلك البعض والنهي بهذا البعض، وإنما يرد على الأشعرية فأجابوا بأن الشيء الصالح للتعلق بالأمور المتعددة قد يتعلق ببعض دون بعض آخر كالقدرة، وفيه أن تعلق الصفة ببعض مع صلوح تعلقها بالكل ترجيح من غير مرجح، وهذا مناف للحكمة ساقط التعلقات فتأمل .
His existence with in 119 The second article on rulings in the Torah: forty years before the creation of Adam: 'And Adam disobeyed his Lord and erred' [Taha:121]. This is information without relation, and it is false. So whatever your answer is, it is our answer. We said: That (i.e., foolishness and frivolity) only follows if the demand (request) in eternity was actual (executed), but we do not say that. Rather, if it is conditional on the attribute of obligation (to be fulfilled in the future), then it does not follow, like the command to the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family and companions) in our right. And by this is refuted what was said: that it is not valid to address the non-existent (al-ma'dum). How not? Indeed, the realization of a relation without the related is impossible necessarily, because relation cannot be realized without the relative. And that (relation) is a relation between the commander and the commanded. And that (refutation) is because the mentioned impossibility is in actual (executed) relation, while intellectual relation does not need the realization of the relative since it is not an actually realized relation; knowledge suffices for it. So reflect, for it is clear, and (he) denies. It was said in answer: فالسفه والعبث are attributes of actions, and al-kayf (how?) and internal speech (kalam nafsi) are attributes, not actions, so they are not described by them; thus the necessity of foolishness and frivolity is denied. I say: No, rather some attributes are also described by them. How not? Command is a request, and request is described by them by consensus. Know that Abdullah bin Sa'id al-Qattan (from) the Ash'aris, i.e., from Ahl al-Sunna wal-Jama'a, and he was advanced over al-Ash'ari (held) freed from this necessity (of foolishness and frivolity) to the view that His speech, exalted, is not in eternity a command or a prohibition or any other of information or interrogation, but rather is described with these in the future after the occurrence of relations and relatives; rather the pre-eternal is the common factor between them, and the divisions are originated. And I have seen the books of some modern scholars that they ruled this opinion to be chosen. And it was objected that these things of command, prohibition, etc. are types of speech, and it is impossible for the genus to exist except within some type, so the pre-eternality of the common factor cannot be conceived. And Abdullah bin Sa'id answered by denying that they are types; rather they are accidents ('awarid) according to the occurrence of relation, which is originated, and it is possible for it to be free of it; and in eternity it was without relation, so it is not in it a command or prohibition. And it can be supported by the fact that His speech is one particular, so it is not a genus applying to different realities. I say: This answer is incomplete. For we conceded that they are not types, but there is no doubt that they are divisions, and the existence of the divided without the existence of some division is impossible, even if the division is according to accidents. And since he said the existence of the divided without these accidents, it follows from him the statement of the existence of some division without these accidents, and that is absurd, inconceivable. Moreover, it contradicts the assumption, for he said the pre-eternal is the common factor: this is a contradiction (khulf). So reflect. Know that His speech, exalted, is one and eternal, with no difference in its essence nor division; rather it is multiple and divided by the multiplicity of relations. And according to what al-Qattan said, that in eternity there is no relation, so there is no multiplicity or division. Yes, it is suitable to become multiple in the future by the occurrence of multiple relations. Indeed, if it were a universal applying to many, it could not exist without some division, and this is very apparent. Then his statement: 'the existence of the divided without some division is impossible' is denied, and if specified by the universal divided, it is not useful. Perhaps this is the meaning in the Hashiya: that there is a difference between division by accidents and after the occurrence of accidents, and here the division is of the second type, and the occurrence of accidents is in the future. So the existence of the divided without divisions in the future is impossible, but the truth is that the intended meaning in communication cannot be conceived without some division, and it is not hidden that the intent of communication in absolute terms in actuality requires the existence of divisions. As for the intent of communication in what will be, it only requires the realization of divisions in it. The secret is that communication only occurs in actual relation, so there is no relation in eternity except in the sense of the validity of benefit, nothing else, and it does not require divisions actually. And you may say: He, exalted, knows in eternity the individual obligated persons, and that at the time of their existence with the conditions of obligation, they are commanded with such and forbidden from such, or He does not know. On the second, it follows that obligation would not be realized in the future either, because Allah did not know that, and it is false. So the first is determined, so intellectual command and prohibition are established, so the existence of some division is necessary. Also, the non-existent is not then obligated, i.e., at the time the speech existed and did not become a command or prohibition or any of the divisions, since there is then no relation of the speech to the act of the obligated. And it may be answered by adhering to the non-existence of the non-existent being obligated in his view, which is corrupt, because the objection of foolishness and frivolity was only about allowing the obligation of the non-existent, so when that is denied, there is no direction for the objection. So the extraction (from the objection) by this face is not valid. Indeed, al-Qattan only said this speech to extract from the mentioned objection. Unless it is said: The Mu'tazila used to raise the objection of foolishness and frivolity against the pre-eternality of speech, so he extracted by this. And the truth is that there is no difference between him and the majority (al-Jumhur) regarding the pre-eternality of conditional obligation (al-taklif al-ta'liqi), as said by the key of divine secrets. Perhaps he meant by the negated command and prohibition the actual (munajjaz) command and prohibition. Then he returns to what the majority held. Then there is no doubt that the occurrence of these accidents in the future is certain, and upon this nothing of the mentioned objections is directed against him. And the Mu'tazila said: If the address (khatab) were eternal, the pre-existence of infinity would follow, for non-existents are infinite, and so what relates to them of address, because the address related to Zayd is different from that related to Amr. The answer: There is no multiplicity in the address related to the essence. Rather the multiplicity that occurs to it according to the multiplicity of relations is a considerational multiplicity, for it (the address) is one eternal attribute with no multiplicity in it like knowledge and power. And its division into types and individuals is according to relations, not by difference of essences, like their division. This. For if you say: Grant that multiplicity in it is considerational, but the relations are not purely invented; rather they have a share of real existence (thubut waqi'i), and the implication (ilzam) that the commands and prohibitions are invented (ikhtira'iyya) leads to infinite regress (tasalsul). I say: The meaning of their being real (waqi'iyya) is that when the address is compared to its relative, it is suitable for the relation to be abstracted from it, not that the relation is an existent thing in determination. So reflect. Then the problem from the beginning is that the obligated persons are limited between the existence of Adam (peace be upon him) and the Day of Resurrection, so they are finite, and likewise the relations. So reflect. And they (the Mu'tazila) said, secondly: If speech were eternal, its relation to everything would be equal. And good and evil according to you (Ash'aris) are revealed (shar'i), so it is suitable to relate to everything, so it would follow that command and prohibition relate to one single act. We say: We do not concede that good and evil are revealed; rather some things are good and some evil. So command relates to that good part and prohibition to this evil part. This objection only applies to the Ash'aris. So they answered: A thing suitable for relation to multiple things may relate to some without others, like power. But there is in it that the attribute's relation to some while it is suitable for relating to all is a preference without a preferrer, and this contradicts wisdom. The relations are null. So reflect.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the usul al-fiqh discussion on the nature of Allah's speech (kalam) and the classification of command (amr) and prohibition (nahy). The author presents the view of Abdullah ibn Sa'id al-Qattan, an Ash'ari scholar, who argues that in eternity, Allah's speech is not actually command or prohibition; rather, those are temporal accidents ('awarid) that occur later when relations (ta'alluqat) arise. The common factor (mushtarak) is the eternal essence of speech, while the divisions (aqsam) are originated (haditha). This is an attempt to avoid the Mu'tazilite objection that eternal command would imply foolishness (safah) and frivolity ('abath) since it would address non-existent beings (ta'liq al-taklif bi'l-ma'dum). The author then critiques al-Qattan's position: if the divisions are not types but accidents, it is still impossible for the divided (al-muqassam) to exist without some division, even if the division is by accidents. The author argues that Allah's speech is one eternal attribute, internally undivided, and multiplicity arises only from the multiplicity of relations, which are temporal. The Hanafi position (al-Jumhur) holds that command and prohibition are real divisions of speech, but they are not separate from the eternal essence; rather, the speech is eternally such that it will become command/prohibition when the relation occurs. This aligns with the concept of 'conditional obligation' (taklif ta'liqi). The passage also addresses the Mu'tazilite objection about infinite regress (tasalsul) and the problem of preference without a preferrer (tarjih bila murajjih). Ultimately, the author concludes that al-Qattan's view can be reconciled with the majority if we understand 'command' and 'prohibition' in his negation to mean actual (munajjaz) command/prohibition, not the potential. Thus the speech is eternal and suitable for relation, but actual commands/prohibitions arise only when the obligated person exists. This is a classic Hanafi defense of the attribute of speech against rationalist objections.

Key Terms
كلام نفسي (kalam nafsi): Internal speech, an eternal attribute of Allah that is not composed of letters or sounds; the source of command, prohibition, etc.
تعلق (ta'alluq): Relation between the divine speech and the acts of obligated persons; this relation is temporal (hadith) according to all, but the potential for relation is eternal.
أمر ونهي (amr wa nahy): Command and prohibition, which are divisions of speech; they are not separate essences but aspects of the one eternal speech that become actual upon relation with an act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abdullah ibn Sa'id al-Qattan, how is Allah's speech in eternity best described?
A) It is already command and prohibition.
B) It is a common factor (mushtarak) without any specific division like command or prohibition.
C) It is composed of multiple distinct types.
D) It is nonexistent until creation.

Key Takeaway
The dispute between Hanafi and Ash'ari (al-Qattan) on the eternality of command and prohibition is largely terminological; both agree on conditional obligation (taklif ta'liqi) and the unity of Allah's speech.

Intoxication (Sukr) as an Acquired Impediment: Definition and Classification
A usul al-fiqh passage defining intoxication and its legal classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify intoxication as permissible or prohibited and identify the legal effects of each category on utterances and confessions, applying Hanafi usul principles.

Core Idea
Intoxication from a permissible source suspends liability; from a prohibited source, it does not excuse — except for apostasy.

In Hanafi usul, intoxication (sukr) is an acquired impediment that affects legal capacity (ahliyya). This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut distinguishes between sukr from permissible and prohibited sources, each with distinct rulings. Understanding this classification is critical for determining the validity of a drunk person's statements — divorce, manumission, oaths, and confessions — and for applying hudud when the person becomes sober. We'll analyze the source text to derive the principles governing these cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of intoxication
The author divides sukr into permissible (from electuaries for medical need, or wine under duress/famine) and prohibited (wine drunk without necessity). Note the basis for permissibility: necessity or medical need.
Permissible sukr is excused due to necessity; prohibited sukr is voluntary and not excused.
2
State the ruling for permissible intoxication
Permissible sukr is treated like ighma' (unconsciousness), which suspends legal liability. The drunk person's statements are not effective.
The author refers to the coming discussion on ighma'.
3
State the ruling for prohibited intoxication
For prohibited sukr, the drunk person is not excused. All utterances (divorce, manumission, oath, zihar) are valid, except for the utterance of apostasy because it requires corruption of belief.
This is the core of the Hanafi position: voluntary intoxication does not nullify legal responsibility.
4
Analyze the exception for apostasy regarding the Prophet
The author notes that in some books, apostasy specifically concerning the Prophet (saw) is effective from a drunk person, and this is relied upon for fatwa. Understand the reasoning: insulting the Prophet is treated as an exceptional case.
This exception shows that the gravity of the offense overrides the general rule.
5
Apply the ruling to confessions and hudud
Confessions are generally accepted except those that are retractable (zina, wine drinking). Confessions of murder and slander lead to retaliation and hadd. Evidence of zina while drunk leads to hadd when sober.
Distinguish between confessions that can be retracted and those that cannot.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها السكر، وهو إما من مباح، كما إذا سكر بالمعاجين التي تؤخذ من أشياء غير الخمر المأكولة لقوة البدن أو بالخمر المشروب وقت الإكراه والمخمصة، وحكمه حكم الإغماء الذي سيجيء إن شاء الله تعالى، وأما من محرم كالخمر المشروب في غير حال الضرورة، وحكمه أنه لا يكون عذراً في حال، فيؤخذ بعباراته حتى يقع طلاقه وعتاقه، ويصح يمينه وظهاره إلا عبارة الردة، إذ ركنها فساد العقيدة ولم يوجد ورأيت في بعض كتب الفقه إلا الردة بسبب الرسول صلوات الله عليه وآله وأصحابه، فإنه يؤخذ به السكران أيضاً، وعليه الاعتماد للفتوى، ويؤخذ بالأقارير إلا الإقرار الذي يصح فيه الرجوع، كالإقرار بالزنا، وشرب الخمر، لا الإقرار بالقتل والقذف فإنه يقتص ويحد، كما إذا قامت البينة على ارتكاب الزنا حال السكر، لكن يحد حال الصحو
And from them (the acquired impediments) is intoxication (sukr). It is either from a permissible source, as when one becomes intoxicated by electuaries that are taken from things other than consumed wine for body strength, or by wine drunk under duress or famine. Its ruling is the ruling of unconsciousness (ighma') which will come if Allah wills. And as for from a prohibited source, like wine drunk without necessity, its ruling is that it is not an excuse at all. His statements are taken into effect so that his divorce and manumission occur, his oath and zihar are valid, except for the statement of apostasy, because its pillar is corruption of belief, and that does not exist. I have seen in some fiqh books that except for apostasy regarding the Messenger (peace be upon him and his family and companions), the drunk person is also taken by it, and upon that is the reliance for fatwa. And his confessions are taken, except for the confession that is subject to retraction, like confession of zina and wine drinking. Not the confession of murder and slander, because he is subject to retaliation and hadd. As when evidence is established on the commission of zina while drunk, but he is subjected to hadd when sober.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage deals with intoxication (sukr) as an acquired impediment to legal capacity. The author distinguishes between sukr from permissible sources (like electuaries for medicinal purposes, or wine under duress/famine) and sukr from prohibited sources (wine drunk without necessity). For permissible sukr, the ruling is like that of unconsciousness (ighma'), which typically suspends legal liability. For prohibited sukr, the drunk person is not excused: his utterances are valid, so divorce, manumission, oaths, and zihar take effect. However, uttering apostasy (ridda) is an exception according to some scholars: because apostasy requires corruption of belief, and the drunk person lacks true belief – but the author notes that in some books, apostasy regarding the Prophet is still effective from a drunk person. Confessions are accepted unless they are retractable (like zina and drinking wine). For confessions of murder and slander, retaliation and hadd apply. Evidence of zina while drunk leads to hadd when sober. This passage reflects the Hanafi position that voluntary intoxication does not exempt one from legal consequences, except where the act inherently requires intent (like apostasy).

Key Terms
السكر (al-sukr): Intoxication; loss of reason due to consumption of intoxicants, here divided into permissible and prohibited
الإغماء (al-ighmā'): Unconsciousness; a state where legal capacity is suspended
الردة (al-ridda): Apostasy; abandonment of Islam

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a drunk person's confession of zina according to the passage?
A) It is valid and he is subjected to hadd immediately.
B) It is not accepted because it is retractable.
C) It is valid only if he was intoxicated from a permissible source.
D) It leads to hadd only if there is evidence.

Key Takeaway
Intoxication from a prohibited source does not nullify legal capacity for most utterances, except apostasy; confessions of crimes like zina are retractable.

Jest (Hazl) in Legal Transactions: Definition and Effect on Sale
Definition and classification of hazl with a case analysis for sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of hazl, classify its domains, and apply the Hanafi rule for hazl in the essence of a sale depending on the parties' agreement.

Core Idea
A contract made in jest is not automatically void — its validity depends on the parties' agreement after the jest.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut unpacks the acquired impediment of jest (hazl) in Hanafi legal theory. While playful words may seem legally inconsequential, the Hanafi school gives weight to the parties' subsequent agreement to either disregard or uphold the transaction. Understanding this distinction is key to correctly applying the rules of contract validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of hazl
Hazl is uttering speech playfully without intending its literal or metaphorical meaning. This distinguishes it from serious speech (jidd) and inadvertence (sahw).
Focus on the core concept: no intention to create legal effects.
2
Classify the domains of hazl
Hazl can occur in initiations (insha'at) like contracts, reports (ikhbarat), or beliefs (i'tiqadat). This lesson focuses on initiations, specifically those subject to rescission like sale.
Other domains have different rulings; not covered here.
3
Analyze the element of jest in a sale
Determine which part of the contract the jest relates to: the essence (asl), the amount of the price (qadr al-badal), or its type (jins). The passage details the case of hazl in the essence.
For hazl in price or type, the ruling may differ; not elaborated here.
4
Determine the outcome based on the parties' agreement
If both parties agree to abandon (i'rad) the jest and treat the contract as never made, the contract is complete (tamm). If they agree to build upon it (bina'), the contract is incomplete, resembling a sale with a perpetual option (khiyar mu'abbad).
'Complete' here means the contract is valid and binding? The text says 'tamm' but context suggests the jest is overlooked and the contract stands. However, the perpetual option analogy indicates a lack of full bindingness. This nuance is important.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها : الهزل، وهو التلفظ بكلام لعباً، ولا يريد معناه الحقيقي ولا المجازي والهزل، إما في إنشاءات أو إخبارات أو اعتقادات، فالأول على أنواع منها ما يحتمل النقض كالبيع، فالهزل إما في أصله أو قدر البدل أو جنسه فإن كان في أصله، فإن اتفقا على الإعراض فالعقد تام وإن اتفقا على البناء فالعقد غير تام، بل هو كالبيع بشرط الخيار المؤبد، فإنهما قد رضيا بالسبب دون الحكم أبداً كما في الخيار المؤبد، فأيهما
And from them (the acquired impediments) is jest (hazl). It is uttering speech playfully, not intending its literal or metaphorical meaning. And hazl is either in initiations (contracts), or reports, or beliefs. The first (initiations) has types: among them what is subject to rescission, like sale. Then hazl is either in its essence, or the amount of the price, or its type. If it is in its essence, then if they both agree on abandoning (the contract), the contract is complete. If they agree on building upon it, the contract is incomplete. Rather, it is like a sale with a perpetual option; they have consented to the cause (i.e., the contract form) without the ruling forever, as in the perpetual option. So whichever (of them)...
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage discusses jest (hazl) as another acquired impediment. The author defines hazl as uttering speech playfully without intending either the literal or metaphorical meaning. He categorizes hazl into three domains: initiations (contracts, etc.), reports (ikhbarat), and beliefs (i'tiqadat). The passage focuses on the first: initiations, specifically those that are subject to rescission like sale. For a sale made 'in jest', the analysis depends on what element of the contract the jest relates to: the essence (asl), the amount of the price (qadr al-badal), or its type (jins). If the jest is in the essence (i.e., the whole contract is jest), then the contract's ruling depends on the parties' agreement: if they both agree to disregard it (al-i'rad), the contract is considered complete (presumably as a valid sale? The text says 'tamm' but likely means the jest is overlooked and the contract stands). If they agree to treat it as a foundation (al-bina'), the contract is not complete; it resembles a sale with a perpetual option (al-khiyar al-mu'abbad), where they consent to the cause (the contract form) but not to the ruling forever. The passage breaks off with 'fayyuhuma' (so whichever...). The implication is that the parties may have certain rights to rescind or enforce. This analysis shows that even in jest, the parties' intentions matter, and Hanafi law does not automatically void such transactions.

Key Terms
الهزل (al-hazl): Jest; playful speech not intended to create legal effects
الإعراض (al-iʿrāḍ): Turning away; agreement to disregard the contract as if not made
البناء (al-binā'): Building upon; agreement to treat the jest as the basis of a valid contract
الخيار المؤبد (al-khiyār al-muʾabbad): Perpetual option; the buyer or seller retains an indefinite right to rescind

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In case of hazl in the essence of a sale, if both parties agree to abandon the jest (i'rad), what is the ruling according to the passage?
A) The contract is void ab initio.
B) The contract is complete (tamm) and binding.
C) The contract is incomplete like a sale with a perpetual option.
D) The contract is valid but each party has an option to rescind.

Key Takeaway
A sale made in jest can become a binding contract if both parties later agree to disregard the jest, or it can become a non-binding contract if they agree to treat it as real.

Jest (Hazl) in Contracts and Its Legal Effect
Usul rule: effect of hazl on insha'at

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for jest (hazl) in contracts by distinguishing between annullable and non-annullable declarations and determining the effect of prior agreement (muwada'a).

Core Idea
Jest in contracts: default validity or default jest? It depends on the type of declaration and party intent.

In this passage, the great Hanafi usuli analyzes how playful utterances (hazl) affect legal declarations. You will see that the effect hinges on whether the contract can be annulled (like sale) or not (like divorce), and on whether parties had a prior agreement (muwada'a) to treat the affair as jest. Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Sahibayn) differ on the default presumption: Abu Hanifa leans toward upholding the contract, while the Sahibayn give weight to the prior jest agreement.

Guided Path
1
Define hazl and its scope
Identify the definition of hazl as playful speech intending neither literal nor figurative meaning. Note that hazl occurs in declarations (insha'), reports (ikhbar), and beliefs (i'tiqad). This lesson focuses on declarations.
Declarations are the primary concern for fiqh and usul.
2
Distinguish annullable vs. non-annullable declarations
Separate declarations that can be annulled (e.g., sale) from those that cannot (e.g., divorce, manumission, oath). The effect of hazl differs: in annullable contracts, hazl can render the contract void or valid depending on intent; in non-annullable contracts, hazl generally has no effect.
Marriage is a special case: it involves wealth but is not annullable.
3
Analyze hazl in sale (case 1: essence of the contract)
For sale, consider three scenarios: both parties agree to disregard (habt), both agree to proceed (bina'), or both remain silent (sukut). Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn disagree on the default.
Study the seventy-two forms of disagreement derived from nine base possibilities.
4
Analyze hazl in the amount and type of price
If hazl is in the amount (excess declared but not intended), Abu Hanifa always upholds the contract (to avoid stipulating a non-price). Sahibayn uphold the jest except when both disregard. If hazl is in the type (e.g., dirhams but say dinars), all agree the contract is considered.
The reason for agreement in type: otherwise the contract would lack a countervalue.
5
Examine hazl in non-annullable declarations and marriage
For divorce, manumission, etc., hazl has no effect due to textual evidence and because they cannot be rescinded. For marriage, if hazl is in the essence, the marriage is binding regardless. If in the dower amount, there is disagreement: Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad say the lesser prevails; Abu Yusuf says the named dower prevails.
Analogical reasoning (qiyas) is used to extend the rule from divorce to other non-annullable declarations.

Source Text

ومنها : الهزل، وهو التلفظ بكلام لعباً، ولا يريد معناه الحقيقي ولا المجازي والهزل، إما في إنشاءات أو إخبارات أو اعتقادات، فالأول على أنواع منها ما يحتمل النقض كالبيع، فالهزل إما في أصله أو قدر البدل أو بطل، وإن أجاز جاز في ثلاثة أيام عنده وفي أي وقت شاء عندهما، وينبغي أن لا تصح الإجازة عند زفر وإن اتفقا في السكوت فالاعتبار للعقد عنده لا للهزل، إذ الأصل فيه أن يكون صحيحاً، وعندهما للهزل، إذ الموجود لا يبطل إلا بمبطل ولا مبطل ها هنا، إذ السكوت ليس إعراضاً، والعذر له أن الإقدام على العقد ناسخ للمواضعة فتأمل، وإن اختلفا في البناء والإعراض أو البناء والسكوت أو السكوت والإعراض، فعنده القول قول من يوجب الصحة، لأن الصحة أصل، وعندهما القول قول المواضعة لأنها أصل عندهما، وفي «التحرير» صور الاتفاق ستة إعراضهما وبناؤهما وسكوتهما وإعراض أحدهما مع بناء الآخر أو مع سكوت الآخر وبناء أحدهما سكوت مع ت الآخر، وصور الاختلاف اثنتان وسبعون، فإما إعراضهما أو بناؤهما أو سكوتهما أو إعراض نفسه بناء صاحبه أو مع سكوته أو مع بناء نفسه إعراض صاحبه أو سكوته أو سكوت نفسه مع إعراض صاحبه أو بنائه فهذه مع تسعة، وإذا أخذ كل واحد منها مع الثمانية الباقية في دعوى الآخر تكون اثنتين وسبعين، هذا: والقول بالصحة مع دعوى كل منهما بناء الآخر دون نفسه بعيد كما لا يخفى على المتأمل، وإن كان الهزل في القدر فالاعتبار للعقد عنده في الصور كلها لأنه لو اعتبر المواضعة في الزائد ويكون الثمن هو الأقل يلزم اشتراط ما ليس بثمن في العقد فيفسد، وحينئذ يلزم إبطال الأصل للوصف وعندهما للهزل إلا في صورة الإعراض منهما، إذ الهزل أصل لا يهدر إلا بمبطل، وإن كان الهزل في جنس الثمن بأن وضعوا أن يكون دراهم ويذكروا دنانير فالعبرة للعقد بالاتفاق، لأنه لو اعتبر الهزل بطل المسمى ويبقى البيع بلا بدل بخلاف الهزل في القدر والبناء عليه، لأنه إذا عمل بالهزل يبقى البيع بأقل الثمن والزيادة وإن كان شرطاً فاسداً إلا أنه لا مطالب له من جهة العبد ولا يورث الفساد ومنها ما لا يحتمل النقض فإما أن لا يكون يلزم فيه المال أصلاً، فلا يؤثر فيه الهزل، كالطلاق والعتاق والرجعة واليمين والعفو عن القصاص للنص في الرجعة والطلاق والنكاح وغيرها مقيس عليها بجامع أنها إنشاءات لا تحتمل الفسخ أو يلزم فيه المال وكان تبعاً كالنكاح فإن كان الهزل في أصل النكاح فالعقد لازم، وإن كان في القدر فإن اتفقا على الإعراض فالمسمى لازم وإن اتفقا على البناء فالأقل بالاتفاق، أما عنده فلأنه يمكن العمل بالهزل ها هنا لأن الأقل يكون مهراً، والزائد شرطاً فاسداً لا يفسد به النكاح، وإن اتفقا على السكوت أو اختلفا ولم يتفقا على شيء فالأقل في رواية الإمام محمد لما بينا، وفي رواية الإمام أبي يوسف المسمى، وفي «التحرير» وهو أصح ، لأن العقل لا يجوز العاقل على الهزل، فكأنهما بدأ بالعقد الجديد، وعندهما الاعتبار للهزل، لأنه هو الأصل عندهما كما مر وإن كان في الجنس فإن اتفقا على الإعراض فالمسمى اتفاقاً أو على البناء، فمهر المثل اتفاقاً لأنه لا مسمى حينئذ، فبقي النكاح بلا بدل، وفيه مهر المثل، وإن اتفقا على السكوت أو اختلفا فمهر المثل عندهما وعنده في رواية الإمام محمد، والمسمى في رواية الإمام أبي يوسف، وقد تقدم الوجهان
And among them is jest (hazl): it is uttering speech playfully, intending neither the literal nor figurative meaning. Jest occurs in declarations (insha'at), reports (ikhbarat), or beliefs (i'tiqadat). The first [declarations] are of types: among them those that can be annulled, like sale. Jest may be in its essence, in the amount of the countervalue, or in its type. If in its essence: if both agree to disregard, the contract is complete; if both agree to proceed, the contract is incomplete, rather it is like a sale with a perpetual option, for they have consented to the cause without the ruling forever, as in the perpetual option. Whichever [party] invalidates it becomes invalid, and if he ratifies, it is valid within three days according to him (Abu Hanifa) and whenever he wants according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Zufar holds that ratification is not valid. If both remain silent: according to him (Abu Hanifa) the contract is considered, not the jest, because the principle is that it is valid; according to them (the two), the jest is considered, for what exists is not nullified without a nullifier, and there is no nullifier here, since silence is not disregard. His (Abu Hanifa's) excuse is that entering into the contract abrogates the prior agreement (muwada'a), so consider. If they differ about proceeding and disregarding, or proceeding and silence, or silence and disregarding: according to him (Abu Hanifa), the word of the one who affirms validity is taken, because validity is the origin; according to them, the word of the prior agreement is taken, because it is the origin with them. In al-Tahrir, the forms of agreement are six: both disregard, both proceed, both silent, one disregards with the other proceeds, or with the other silent, one proceeds with the other silent. The forms of disagreement are seventy-two: either both disregard, or both proceed, or both silent, or one disregards and the other proceeds, or one disregards and the other silent, or one proceeds and the other silent, or one proceeds and the other disregards, or one silent and the other disregards, or one silent and the other proceeds — these are nine. When each is taken with the remaining eight in the claim of the other, that makes seventy-two. This: the view of validity when each claims the other proceeded but not himself is far-fetched, as is not hidden from the contemplative. If the jest is in the amount: according to him (Abu Hanifa), the contract is considered in all cases, because if the prior agreement (muwada'a) were considered regarding the excess and the price becomes the lesser, it would entail stipulating something that is not part of the price in the contract, which invalidates; then the invalidation of the essence for the description would follow. According to them (the two), the jest is considered except in the case of both disregarding, because jest is an origin not nullified except by a nullifier. If the jest is in the type of price — for example, they agreed it would be dirhams but mention dinars — then the contract is considered by agreement, because if the jest were considered, the named price would be void and the sale would remain without a countervalue, unlike jest in amount and proceeding upon it, because if the jest is acted upon, the sale remains with the lesser price, and the excess, though an invalid condition, cannot be claimed by the slave side and does not cause corruption. And among them (declarations) are those that cannot be annulled. Either they do not involve wealth at all, so jest does not affect them, like divorce, manumission, revocation (ruj'a), oath, and pardon for retaliation — due to the textual evidence for revocation, divorce, marriage, and others analogized to them because they are declarations that cannot be rescinded. Or they involve wealth but as a subsidiary, like marriage. If the jest is in the essence of marriage, the contract is binding. If in the amount: if both agree to disregard, the named [dower] is binding; if both agree to proceed, the lesser by agreement. According to him (Abu Hanifa), it is possible to act on the jest here because the lesser becomes the dower, and the excess is an invalid condition that does not invalidate marriage. If both are silent or differ without agreement: the lesser according to Imam Muhammad's narration, as we explained; according to Imam Abu Yusuf's narration, the named [dower]; in al-Tahrir, the latter is more correct, because the rational person does not jest about marriage, so it is as if they began a new contract. According to them (the two), the jest is considered, because it is the origin as mentioned. If the jest is in the type [of dower]: if both agree to disregard, the named [dower] by agreement; if both agree to proceed, the mahr al-mithl by agreement because there is no named dower then, so the marriage remains without a countervalue, and mahr al-mithl is due. If both are silent or differ: according to them and according to him (Abu Hanifa) in Imam Muhammad's narration, mahr al-mithl; according to Imam Abu Yusuf's narration, the named [dower]; the two views have preceded.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a detailed Hanafi analysis of jest (hazl) in contractual declarations. It first defines hazl as uttering words playfully without intending literal or figurative meaning. Hazl occurs in declarations (insha'), reports, and beliefs. The focus is on declarations that can be annulled, like sale. The passage examines three scenarios: hazl in the essence of the contract, in the amount of the countervalue, and in the type of countervalue. Throughout, there is a disagreement between Abu Hanifa („عنه“) and the two disciples („عندهما“) regarding whether the actual intent (the „muwada'a“ or prior agreement) or the apparent contract is given effect. Abu Hanifa leans toward upholding the contract as valid unless both parties clearly intend otherwise, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider the prior agreement as the default. The passage enumerates many possible combinations of agreement and disagreement. It then moves to contracts that cannot be annulled, such as divorce and manumission (no financial element), where hazl has no effect. For marriage, which involves wealth but as subsidiary, if hazl is in the essence, the contract is binding. If hazl is in the dower amount, there are further details and disagreements among Imam Muhammad, Abu Yusuf, and Abu Hanifa. The text relies heavily on the concept of 'muwada'a' (prior collusion) to determine the effect.

Key Terms
هزل (hazl): Jest or playful utterance without intending the literal or figurative meaning.
مواضعة (muwada'a): A prior agreement or collusion between parties to treat the transaction as jest.
إنشاء (insha'): Declarations that bring about a legal effect (e.g., sale, marriage, divorce).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the effect of jest in non-annullable declarations like divorce?
A) The divorce is void
B) The divorce is valid and jest has no effect
C) The divorce is suspended pending ratification
D) The divorce is valid only if both parties intended it

Key Takeaway
Jest in declarations is evaluated based on the type of declaration and the parties' intent; the Hanafi school has a detailed framework with intra-school differences on the default presumption.

Hajr of Terminal Illness and Death in Hanafi Usul
Usul exposition on hajr of illness and death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of marad al-mawt as a type of hajr, explain the effect of death on the dhimmah, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on kafalah after death.

Core Idea
Marad al-mawt limits gratuitous acts; death extinguishes the dhimmah; kafalah requires a claimable principal.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut treats two types of legal interdiction (hajr): terminal illness and death. In Hanafi usul, marad al-mawt restricts the sick person's capacity to make donations to protect creditors and heirs. Death dissolves all moral responsibility (taklif), leaving only obligations tied to specific assets. The passage concludes with an intra-Hanafi dispute over the validity of kafalah (suretyship) for a debt of a deceased who left no assets. Understanding these rules reveals how liability (dhimmah) functions in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nature of marad as hajr
The passage first states that sickness (marad) is a type of incapacity but does not negate comprehension or capacity for worship. Then it explains that because it is a cause of death, the sick person is interdicted from gratuitous transactions (tabarru'at) beyond one-third of his wealth, to protect creditors (full wealth) and heirs (two-thirds). Note that this hajr applies only if death follows.
Not all sickness creates hajr; only marad al-mawt (terminal illness) does.
2
Examine the effect of death on liability
Death demolishes the foundation of taklif. Nothing remains on the deceased's liability except matters tied to specific objects (like deposits or usurped property) that can be reclaimed from the estate. Debts and legacies are paid from the estate, with legacies taking precedence over debts by consensus.
After death, no new obligations can arise; only pre-existing rights against specific assets survive.
3
Analyze the kafalah dispute
The text presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether kafalah for a debt of a deceased with no assets is valid. Abu Hanifah says no, because kafalah is defined as joining a liability to another in claim (dam al-dhimmah ila al-dhimmah fi al-mutalabah). Since there is no claim against the deceased (no assets), no joining can occur. The other view (likely of the Sahibayn) holds it valid because joining occurs in the debt itself. The text prefers Abu Hanifah's view as per al-Hidayah.
The dispute hinges on the definition of kafalah: is it joining in claim or in the debt itself?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها المرض، وهو نوع من العجز ولا ينافي فهم الخطاب وأهلية العبادات، ولذا لا ينافي التكليف إلا أنه لما كان نوعاً من العجز شرعت العبادات على حسب المكنة وأخر ما لا قدرة عليه أو ما فيه حرج، ثم هو سبب للموت، وهو سبب الخلافة في المال، ولذا حجر المريض عن التبرعات والتصرفات المشتملة عليها في كل المال لحق الغرماء والثلثين لحق الورثة، لكن إذا اتصل به الموت، وأما التصرفات التي ليس فيها تبرع كالبيع بمثل القيمة والنكاح بمهر المثل لا يمنع منه، والشرع إذ أبطل التوارث علمنا أنه يتعلق بالنظر إليه حق الورثة في الصورة أيضاً، فمنعنا من الإقرار له والبيع معه ، ثم إنه تفسخ العقود المحجورة عليه إن كانت قابلة للفسخ، وإلا فحكمها حكم المعلق كإعتاق العبد من التركة المستغرقة بالدين أو قيمته تزيد على الثلث، فإنه يعتق بعد الموت، ويسعى في قيمته في الأول والزائد على الثلث في الثاني، هذا : ومنها الموت. مسألة، الموت هادم لأساس التكليف لأنه عن إتيان العبادات أداء وقضاء، ولأنه كله عجز ذهب من دار الابتلاء إلى دار الجزاء فلا يبقى على ذمة الميت إلا ما كان متعلقاً بعين) لعل إلا ها هنا صفة بمعنى غير هو فاعل لا يبقى، ولا يصح أن يكون استثناء مفرغاً متصلاً، فإنه ليس على ذمة الميت ما كان متعلقاً بعين أيضاً، ولا أن يكون منقطعاً أيضاً، لأنه مفرغ يصح فالحاصل أنه لا يبقى على ذمة الميت غير المتعلق بعين كالعبادات مالية كانت أو بدنية، وأما المتعلق بعين أو مال فلا يبقى على ذمته أيضاً، لكن لصاحب الحق أن يأخذه من العين أو المال كالودائع والغصوب) فإن للمودع والمغصوب منه أن يأخذه كما كان في الحياة وعلى الورثة أن يردوه (أو) غير ما كان متعلقاً بمال تركه كالديون فإن الدائنين لهم أن يأخذوها منه، وعلى الورثة أن لا يتصرفوا من دون الأداء والوصايا) فإن الموصى له يكون خليفة في ملك الثلث والتجهيز ويقدم) على الديون والوصايا (بالإجماع) وإذا لم يبق في ذمة الميت شيء أصلاً فلا تصح الكفالة بما عليه من الدين (بعد الموت عند من الدين ( بعد الموت عند أبي حنيفة) إذا لم يترك وفاء من المال (لأنها ) أي الكفالة ضم الذمة إلى الذمة في المطالبة فيجوز للدائن مطالبة أيهما شاء (ولا (مطالبة ها هنا على الأصيل فلا ضم) فيها قال مطلع الأسرار قدس سره: ها هنا قولان: الأول : أن الكفالة ضم الذمة إلى الذمة في المطالبة، والآخر أنها ضم الذمة إلى الذمة في هذا الاستدلال إلا إذا ترجح القول الأول ، وما في «الهداية» الأول أصح دعوى الدين، فلا يتم
And among them is sickness (marad), which is a type of incapacity and does not contradict comprehension of address (fahm al-khitab) and capacity for worship. Therefore, it does not contradict moral responsibility (taklif), except that because it is a type of incapacity, acts of worship are prescribed according to ability, and what is beyond ability or involves hardship is postponed. Then it is a cause of death, and death is a cause of succession in wealth. Therefore, the sick person is interdicted from voluntary donations and transactions that include them entirely in his wealth for the right of creditors, and in two-thirds for the right of heirs, but only if it is connected with death. As for transactions that do not involve donation, such as a sale for equivalent value and marriage with a proper dower, he is not prevented from them. And since the law has nullified inheritance, we know that the right of the heirs is connected to consideration of it in form as well, so we prevent him from making an acknowledgment or sale with it. Then, the contracts that are subject to interdiction are rescinded if they are susceptible to rescission; otherwise, their ruling is like a suspended ruling, as in the case of freeing a slave from the estate that is entirely consumed by debt or whose value exceeds one-third. For then, the slave becomes free after death and must work to pay his value in the first case, and the excess over one-third in the second case. That is it. And among them is death. Issue: Death demolishes the foundation of moral responsibility, because it prevents the performance of acts of worship (ada' and qada') and because it is total incapacity; one goes from the abode of trial to the abode of recompense. Therefore, nothing remains on the liability of the deceased except what is connected to a specific object (mulhq bi 'ayn). Perhaps 'illa' here is a description meaning 'other than'? It is the subject of 'la yabqa'. It is not correct for it to be a continuous absolute exception, for there is not on the deceased's liability what is connected to a specific object either. Nor can it be a disconnected exception, because it is a valid absolute exception. The conclusion is that nothing remains on the deceased's liability other than what is not connected to a specific object, such as acts of worship, whether financial or physical. As for what is connected to a specific object or property, it also does not remain on his liability; but the right-holder may take it from the object or property, as in the case of deposits and usurpations, for the depositor and the one from whom something was usurped may take it as in life, and the heirs must return it. Or other than what is not connected to the property he left behind, like debts, for the creditors may take them from it. And the heirs must not dispose of the property without payment, and legacies, for the legatee becomes a successor in ownership of the one-third and equipment. And (the legacy) is given precedence over debts and legacies by consensus. And if nothing remains on the deceased's liability at all, then suretyship (kafalah) for the debt due from him is not valid after death according to Abu Hanifah, if he has left no means of payment from the property. Because suretyship is the joining of a liability to a liability in terms of claim, so the creditor may demand payment from whichever he wishes. And here there is no claim against the principal (the deceased), so there is no joining. Matali' al-Asrar (may Allah sanctify his secret) said: Here there are two views: the first is that suretyship is the joining of a liability to a liability in the claim; the other is that it is the joining of a liability to a liability in this argument? But if the first view is preponderant, and what is in al-Hidayah is that the first is more correct. Claim of debt, so it is not complete.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage treats two additional types of hajr (legal interdiction): sickness (marad) and death (mawt). In the Hanafi school, a sick person in his final illness (marad al-mawt) is interdicted from making donations or transactions that exceed one-third of his wealth, to protect the rights of creditors and heirs. The text clarifies that this hajr applies only if the sickness leads to death. Transactions that are not donations, such as a sale at fair value or marriage with proper dower, are not prevented. Contracts that violate the hajr may be rescinded or treated as suspended, like freeing a slave whose value exceeds one-third. The discussion on death explains that death terminates all religious obligations (taklif). Nothing remains on the deceased's liability except matters tied to specific objects (like deposits or usurped property), which can be reclaimed from the estate. Debts and legacies are to be paid from the estate, with legacies from one-third after debt. Finally, a specific ruling from Abu Hanifah: kafalah (suretyship) for a debt owed by the deceased is invalid after death if the deceased left no assets, because there is no claim against the principal (the deceased) to which the guarantor's liability can be attached. The text quotes from Matali' al-Asrar and al-Hidayah to confirm the first view as the correct one. The OCR corruption makes some parts difficult, but the main rulings are discernible.

Key Terms
المرض (al-marad): Sickness, especially terminal illness (marad al-mawt), which triggers legal interdiction for gratuitous acts.
الموت (al-mawt): Death, which terminates all moral responsibility (taklif) and leaves only obligations tied to specific assets.
الكفالة (al-kafalah): Suretyship; the act of joining one's liability to that of another for the purpose of claim.
الذمة (al-dhimmah): Liability; the abstract legal capacity that renders a person liable for debts and obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifah as cited in the passage, why is kafalah (suretyship) for the debt of a deceased person invalid if the deceased left no assets?
A) Because the deceased is no longer alive to consent.
B) Because there is no claim (mutalabah) against the deceased, so there is nothing to which the guarantor's liability can be joined.
C) Because the heirs have already paid the debt.
D) Because kafalah is only valid for living persons.

Key Takeaway
Marad al-mawt creates a limited hajr on gratuitous acts; death extinguishes the dhimmah; kafalah after death is invalid per Abu Hanifah because it requires a claimable principal.

The Hanafi Classification of Words: Ism, Fi‘l, Harf Based on Independence of Meaning
Defining ism, fi‘l, harf through istiqlal and time indication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three parts of speech (ism, fi‘l, harf) using the Hanafi criterion of istiqlal (independence of meaning) and explain why fi‘l is independent only at the level of tadammun.

Core Idea
A word's classification depends on whether its meaning is self-sufficient; fi‘l is independent in event but not in time and relation.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut lays the foundational Hanafi classification of ism, fi‘l, and harf. The criterion is not purely grammatical but conceptual: istiqlal (independence of meaning). Understanding this classification is essential because it underpins the usul al-fiqh analysis of Quranic and hadith texts — whether a word can be a subject or predicate, affecting how rulings are derived.

Guided Path
1
Identify the criterion
The passage uses istiqlal (independence of meaning) as the primary classification criterion. Words are divided based on whether their meaning is self-sufficient when observed by itself.
Istiqlal is the key concept.
2
Apply the criterion to each part of speech
Ism has independent meaning; harf has non-independent meaning (only signifies in relation to others); fi‘l indicates time via its form, but its meaning is not fully independent because it contains a relation (nisba) and time (zaman).
3
Analyze fi‘l's dual independence
Fi‘l is independent on the tadammuni (implicit) level — the event meaning — but non-independent on the mutabiqi (literal) level because it includes time and relation.
This distinction is crucial for understanding fi‘l's grammatical behavior.
4
Follow the debate on fi‘l as predicate
The author considers and refutes two alternative explanations for how fi‘l functions as a predicate: metaphorical use for the event alone, or literal use with the event as predicate.
Pay attention to the critique of the metaphorical view.
5
Evaluate the author's conclusion
The author concludes that fi‘l's event meaning is independent on the tadammuni level, allowing it to be predicate but not subject, because the event is always attributed to an agent.
This reasoning resolves the issue of how a non-independent word can function as khabar.

And the singulative is ism, fi'l, and harf because its meaning is either independent (in conceptuality and that) i.e., independence (if it is observed by itself without being observed as a mirror for another and a state of its states (so it is suitable for being judged upon and judging with) (or) it is not independent) its meaning but rather is an instrument for observing another and a mirror for knowing its state) i.e., sometimes the meaning is observed primarily and essentially and sometimes it is observed as a state of the states of another meaning and a relation between two meanings, so it is observed by observing that other subsequently. Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a detailed definitional discussion of the three parts of speech: ism (noun), fi'l (verb), and harf (particle). The classification is based on the concept of istiqlal (independence) of meaning and indication of time. Ism has an independent meaning, harf has a dependent meaning (it only signifies in relation to others), and fi'l indicates time through its form but its meaning is not fully independent because it includes a relational aspect. The author argues that fi'l is independent on the level of tadammun (implicit meaning) i.e., the event, but not on the level of mutabaqa (literal correspondence). There is a discussion on whether the sentence can be news (khabar) despite containing non-independent elements. The author refutes the view that the verb is used metaphorically for the event alone, emphasizing that time and relation are always understood.

Key Terms
استقلال (istiqlal): The quality of a word's meaning being self-sufficient, i.e., able to be judged upon or to judge with without needing another word.
تضمني (tadammuni): Implicit meaning; the partial meaning that is included in the total meaning of a word, e.g., the event in a verb.
مطابقي (mutabiqi): Literal corresponding meaning; the full meaning that a word indicates by coinage.
فعل (fi‘l): A word that indicates an event and one of the three times through its form.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the verb (fi‘l) not independent on the literal (mutabiqi) level?
A) Because it indicates an event that is always relational.
B) Because it includes time and relation, which are non-independent.
C) Because it cannot be used as a predicate.
D) Because it is composed of letters that indicate parts.

Key Takeaway
The classification of words in Hanafi usul depends on independence of meaning; fi‘l is independent only in its implicit event meaning, not literally.

The Verb and Its Analytic Parts
Exposition of the verb's nature and its analytic decomposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three analytic components of the verb (event, time, relation) and describe their respective epistemic independence.

Core Idea
The verb's meaning is not a simple event; it fuses event, time, and relation into one integral whole.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, understanding the linguistic structure of the verb is essential for deriving rulings from revealed texts. This passage from 'Fawatih al-Rahmut' dissects the verb into its constitutive parts and explains how these parts relate in usage and analysis.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish material and form
Identify that the verb's material (madda) signifies the event, and its form (hay'a) signifies attribution to something else in a specific time.
2
Recognize the three post‑analysis components
After analysis, the verb yields event, time, and relation. Note that the relation is non‑independent, the event is independent, and time is independent by itself but dependent as a container for the relation.
This analysis is based on the work 'Matali' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyya'.
3
Understand integral fusion in actual usage
In ordinary discourse, the verb conveys one integral meaning from which the parts are inseparable; implicative and literal meanings coincide.
4
Apply to istinbat
When interpreting a Qur'anic or hadith verb, a Hanafi usuli recognizes that the verb inherently includes time and relation, which may affect the ruling's scope (e.g., obligations tied to time).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And it is supported by the fact that the singular word conveys only one integral meaning, and there is no doubt in the validity of its being predicated and independent, so reflect. (And the compound, if it conveys a complete sense upon which it is permissible to stop, it is a sentence, and it is constituted by two nouns: one being the predicate and the other the subject, or a noun being the subject and a verb being the predicate, since it necessarily requires predication established between the subject and predicate. And this ruling is invalidated by your saying 'O Zaid' because it is a sentence permitting stopping, composed of a particle and a noun. And it is answered that it is not conceded that it is composed of a particle and a noun, but rather it is of a verb? A complete benefit? The well-known? with that it is he is implied and a noun, and (that) the particle is a deputy for the verb transferred from declarative to performative request. This is the grammarians. And some grammarians went that there is no transfer here, but the vocative form is a verb-noun coined for performative request, and the opener of divine secrets chose it for being safer from artificialities. And know that the compounding of the compound is for benefiting) i.e., for benefiting what is not already obtained, and the compounding of the singular is for reminding) i.e., for reminding what was previously obtained and forgotten. (Otherwise) i.e., if the compounding of the singular were not for reminding but for benefiting, then circularity would follow, for knowledge of the coinage of the word for the meaning is a condition of its indication, so knowledge of the meaning from the word depends on this knowledge, and this knowledge depends on knowledge of the meaning, so knowledge of the meaning from the word depends on knowledge of the meaning, so if the meaning were benefited by the word, knowledge of the meaning would depend on knowing it from the word, which is circularity. (And there is something in it since in the coinage of the general for the general, knowledge of the particular meaning is not necessary), then it is permissible that what is benefited from the singular be a meaning not previously obtained, and this benefit depends on knowledge of the coinage for it depending on knowledge of the meaning in another way, so there is no other way, so no circularity. And also these premises apply to the compound except that it may be said that the condition of its indication is knowledge of the coinage of its parts for their meanings, not knowledge of its coinage for its compositional meaning, so reflect.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is a detailed definitional analysis of the verb (الفعل) as treated in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author first distinguishes between the material (مادة) of the verb, which signifies the event, and its form (هيئة), which signifies attribution to something else in a specific time. The two together yield the composite meaning. The work 'مطلع الأسرار الإلهية' is then cited to argue that the verb's meaning is an integral whole that can be analyzed into three components: event (حدث), time (زمان), and relation (نسبة). The relation is not independent, while the event is independent; the time is independent if considered by itself but not if considered as a container for the relation. The author emphasizes that in actual usage the verb conveys a single, independent meaning attributed to the agent, and its parts are fused so that implicative and literal meanings coincide. The passage then turns to define the sentence (جملة) as a compound that yields complete sense, constituted by a subject and a predicate. An objection is raised using the vocative 'يا زيد', which some argue breaks the definition because it consists of a particle and a noun. The response clarifies that the particle stands in for a verb, and some grammarians even consider the vocative form itself as verb-noun. Finally, the passage discusses the purpose of coinage: compounds are coined to convey new information (إفادة), while singular words are coined to remind of known information (إعادة). This distinction avoids circularity in the theory of meaning. The author concludes by noting that in the case of general coinage (وضع العام للعام), knowledge of the particular meaning is not required, which prevents circularity.

Key Terms
الفعل (al-fi'l): A word whose material signifies an event and whose form signifies attribution to something else in a specific time; in analysis, it comprises event, time, and relation.
المادة (al-madda): The root of the verb that carries the lexical meaning of the event.
الهيئة (al-hay'a): The morphological form of the verb that indicates the time and the relation of attribution.
الحدث (al-hadath): The event itself, the core meaning carried by the madda.
الزمان (al-zaman): The time dimension expressed by the verb's form (past, present, future).
النسبة (al-nisba): The relation between the event and the agent, also indicated by the verb's form.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which component of the verb is considered non‑independent in the analytic state?
A) The event
B) The time
C) The relation
D) Both event and time

Key Takeaway
The verb in Hanafi usul is an integral whole that, upon analysis, separates into event, time, and relation, enabling precise derivation of time‑bound obligations.

Purpose of Coinage: Singular for Reminding, Compound for Informing
Exposition on the purpose of coinage for singular and compound expressions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why singular words are coined for reminding (i'ada) and compounds for benefiting (ifada), and evaluate the circularity objection.

Core Idea
Singular words remind of known meanings; compounds convey new information.

This passage from 'Fawatih al-Rahmut' explains a fundamental principle in the philosophy of language: words are coined either to remind of already known meanings (i'ada) or to inform of new meanings (ifada). This distinction is critical in usul al-fiqh for understanding how revealed texts convey obligations.

Guided Path
1
Understand the distinction
Recognize that a compound (murakkab) such as a sentence is coined to convey new information (ifada), while a singular word (mufrad) is coined to remind (i'ada) of meanings already known.
The passage states: 'وضع المركب للإفادة ووضع المفرد للإعادة'.
2
Identify the circularity argument
If a singular word were for ifada, then knowing the meaning from the word would require prior knowledge of the meaning, leading to infinite regress. The passage presents this problem and its solution.
3
Analyze the solution
The solution is that coinage can be general (وضع العام للعام); one does not need to know the particular meaning beforehand. Additionally, compounds are understood through knowledge of their parts, not through a separate coinage of the whole.
4
Apply to usul
In interpreting the Qur'an and Sunnah, singular words (like 'salat' or 'zakat') remind us of the established meanings from revelation, while compound sentences provide new legal rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage is a detailed definitional analysis of the verb (الفعل) as treated in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author first distinguishes between the material (مادة) of the verb, which signifies the event, and its form (هيئة), which signifies attribution to something else in a specific time. The two together yield the composite meaning. The work 'مطلع الأسرار الإلهية' is then cited to argue that the verb's meaning is an integral whole that can be analyzed into three components: event (حدث), time (زمان), and relation (نسبة). The relation is not independent, while the event is independent; the time is independent if considered by itself but not if considered as a container for the relation. The author emphasizes that in actual usage the verb conveys a single, independent meaning attributed to the agent, and its parts are fused so that implicative and literal meanings coincide. The passage then turns to define the sentence (جملة) as a compound that yields complete sense, constituted by a subject and a predicate. Key Terms
الإفادة (al-ifada): Conveying new information that was not previously known; the purpose of compounding.
الإعادة (al-i'ada): Reminding of a meaning that was known before; the purpose of singular coinage.
الدور (al-dawr): Logical circularity that would occur if singular words were for ifada: knowledge of meaning depends on knowledge of coinage, which depends on meaning.
وضع العام للعام (wad' al-'amm li'l-'amm): The coinage of a general word for a general concept, without specifying particular instances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the resolution to the circularity objection if singular words were for ifada?
A) Singular words are actually for i'ada, so the objection does not arise.
B) The objection is accepted and no resolution is given.
C) The resolution is that compounds are only for i'ada, not ifada.
D) The resolution is that general coinage (وضع العام للعام) allows new information without requiring prior knowledge of particular meaning.

Key Takeaway
Singular words remind of known meanings, while compounds convey new rulings; this distinction, supported by the concept of general coinage, ensures a sound theory of linguistic communication in usul.

Types of Wad': Specific for Specific (Khas li Khas)
Defines the first type of wad'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define specific-specific coinage (خاص لخاص) and distinguish between its universal and particular objects.

Core Idea
In specific-specific coinage, both word and meaning are observed in their particularity; the object may be universal or particular.

The science of usul al-fiqh begins with understanding how words convey meanings. One foundational classification is the division of linguistic coinage (al-wad') into types based on the relationship between the word and its meaning. This lesson examines the first type: specific for specific, where the coinage is tailored to a particular word and a particular meaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of coinage
Read the text to understand that this is the 'specific for specific' type. The word and meaning are both observed in their specificity.
The text uses the example of 'Zaid' and 'man' to illustrate.
2
Analyze the coining perspective
Note that in this type, the coiner looks at the word and meaning individually, not as general categories. The specificity is in both the word and its assigned meaning.
3
Determine the nature of the object (موضوع له)
The object may be universal (كلي) like 'man' or particular (جزئي) like 'Zaid'. Recognize that this type covers both proper nouns and common nouns.
The text says: 'وفيه إشارة إلى أن هذا القسم قد يكون الموضوع له فيه كلياً وقد يكون جزئياً'
4
Apply to examples
Take 'Zaid': it is coined for a specific individual, so the object is particular. Take 'man': it is coined for a universal concept (the species), so the object is universal. Both fall under the same type.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
